gb-headline-text">|</div><div class="gb-headline gb-headline-385678fb gb-headline-text dynamic-term-class"><span class="post-term-item term-howtos"><a href="https://kifarunix.com/howtos/">HowTos</a></span>, <span class="post-term-item term-at-batch"><a href="https://kifarunix.com/howtos/automate-system-tasks/at-batch/">at/batch</a></span>, <span class="post-term-item term-automate-system-tasks"><a href="https://kifarunix.com/howtos/automate-system-tasks/">Automate System Tasks</a></span></div><div class="gb-headline gb-headline-61a02fee gb-headline-text">|</div><div class="gb-headline gb-headline-7b6af61f gb-headline-text"><a href="https://kifarunix.com/scheduling-tasks-using-at-command-in-linux/#comments">1 Comment</a></div></div></header><div class="entry-content" itemprop="text"><p>Our previous two guides, whose links are below, we covered how to schedule system tasks or jobs in Linux using the <code>cron</code> and <code>anacron</code> commands. This guide will focus on scheduling tasks using <code>at</code> command in Linux systems.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-901" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="901" style="max-width:100%!important;float:none!important;margin-right:auto!important;margin-left:auto!important;min-width:728px;min-height:90px;line-height:0;padding:0;margin-top:15px!important;margin-bottom:15px!important;display:block!important;text-align:center!important"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-105" data-inserter-version="2"></span><p><a href="https://kifarunix.com/how-to-schedule-cron-jobs-tasks-in-linux-unix/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener" aria-label="(opens in a new tab)">How to Schedule Cron Jobs/Tasks in Linux/Unix</a></p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-142" data-inserter-version="2"></span><p><a rel="noreferrer noopener" aria-label="(opens in a new tab)" href="https://kifarunix.com/scheduling-tasks-using-anacron-in-linux-unix/" target="_blank">Scheduling tasks using anacron in Linux/Unix</a></p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-150" data-inserter-version="2"></span><h2 class="wp-block-heading">Schedule tasks using at command in Linux</h2><p><code>at</code> utility is used to schedule a one-time task. These are the tasks that are executed only once at a specific time.<br><code>at</code> reads commands from standard input or from the file that is specified using the <code>-f</code> option.<br>Jobs scheduled using <code>at</code> are executed by the <code>atd</code> service.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-151" data-inserter-version="2"></span><h3 class="wp-block-heading">Scheduling tasks using at command</h3><p>The at command ordinarily expects time as the argument.<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at TIME</code></pre><p>Where TIME can be specified using keywords such as;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-152" data-inserter-version="2"></span><ul class="wp-block-list"><li><code>noon</code>, <code>midnight</code> or <code>teatime (4:00 PM)</code>,<li><code>next week</code>, <code>tomorrow</code>, <code>teatime tomorrow</code>, <code>next tuesday</code>,<code>next Tue</code>, <code>next Tuesday</code>, <code>next month</code>.</ul><p>When executed with no commands or scripts passed to it, <code>at</code> commands runs interactively and expects you to enter the commands to execute from the prompt.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-909" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="909" style="margin-left:auto!important;display:block!important;float:none!important;margin-top:15px!important;margin-bottom:15px!important;min-width:728px;border:0 solid #ddd!important;max-width:728px;line-height:0;padding:0;margin-right:auto!important;text-align:center!important;min-height:400px;width:728px"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-153" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 11 PM Dec 2
at&gt;</code></pre><p>At the prompt, enter the command to run. For example;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 11 PM Dec 2
at&gt; echo &#34;This is a test at Job &gt; /tmp/test-at-job&#34;</code></pre><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 11 PM Dec 2
at&gt; df -hT</code></pre><p>When done typing commands, press Ctrl+D to terminate input. When you press Ctrl+D, you will see <code>&lt;EOT></code> at the command line.<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 11 PM Dec 2
at&gt; df -hT<eot></eot></code></pre><p>You can as well pass the commands to execute to at command from command line by specifying the file with commands using the <code>-f</code> option. For example, consider a file called <code>mycommands.sh</code> with two shell scripts</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-910" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="910"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-154" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-code"><code>cat mycommands.sh
/home/me/myscripts/clean-tmp.sh
/home/me/myscripts/backup.sh</code></pre><p>To have at execute these commands next week the same day at midnight;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at -f mycommands.sh midnight next week</code></pre><p>You can as well use the standard input redirection symbol;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at teatime next month &lt; mycommands.sh</code></pre><p>You can also pipe tasks/commands to <code>at</code> command. For example to create a notification using the <code>notify-send</code> command,</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-911" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="911"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-122" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>echo &#39;notify-send &#34;You need to refill the gas&#34;&#39; -t 1000 | at 17:00</code></pre><p>This will send you a notification at 5 PM to refill the gas.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-709" data-method="ai-placeholders" class="ezoic-autoinsert-ad"></span><p><strong>NOTE:</strong><ul class="wp-block-list"><li>For all the <code>at</code> examples that follows below, you can either pass the the commands or scripts or tasks/jobs to be executed to at command or you can interactively enter them.<span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-155" data-inserter-version="2"></span></ul><p>To run the job one week from today, same time as when the at job was scheduled;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-112" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at next week</code></pre><p>To run the job at 4 PM tomorrow<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at teatime tomorrow</code></pre><p>Run a job on next Tuesday, same time as when the job was scheduled.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-912" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="912"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-156" data-inserter-version="2"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-602" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at next tue</code></pre><p>Run the job next month, same date at midnight.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-110" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at midnight next month</code></pre><ul class="wp-block-list"><li>using the keyword <code>now</code> plus a time period. For example, if to schedule a task to run 4 hours from now, use the time period <code>now + 4 hours</code>.<li>For example;<br>To run the job today at 4PM plus 2 hours, that is at 6PM<span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-157" data-inserter-version="2"></span></ul><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 4PM + 2 hours</code></pre><p>To run the job one and half hour from now;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at now + 90 minutes</code></pre><p>To run the job two minutes from now;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at now + 2 minutes</code></pre><p>To run a job next on monday 2 hours after the same time when the job was scheduled;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-158" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at monday + 2 hours</code></pre><ul class="wp-block-list"><li>using a time of the day either in <code>24-hour</code> or <code>12-hour</code> clock system. For example; <code>16:00</code> or <code>4:00 PM</code>.<li>For example;<br>To run the job at 5PM today;</ul><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 5:00 PM or at 5 PM or at 17:00</code></pre><ul class="wp-block-list"><li>using <code>time of the day</code> and <code>date</code>.<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>The date can be specified in the format <code>DD.MM.YY</code>, <code>MMDDYY</code> or <code>MM/DD/YY</code>.<li><code>MONTH Date, Year</code> or <code>MONTH Date Year</code> or <code>MONTH Date</code>. You can write the first three letters of the month e.g <code>Jan</code> or <code>jan</code>.<li>For example,<br>To run the job on first october, year 2019 same time as when the job was scheduled</ul><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-111" data-inserter-version="2"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-159" data-inserter-version="2"></span></ul><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 12:30 PM 10/01/19 or at 12:30 PM 01.10.19 or at 12:30 PM 100119</code></pre><p>To run the job on 2nd Jan, 2020 same time as when the job was scheduled<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at Jan 1, 2020 ot at Jan 1 2020</code></pre><p>To run the job at 11 PM on 2nd Dec, this year;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-913" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="913"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at 11 PM Dec 2</code></pre><h3 class="wp-block-heading">List scheduled at jobs</h3><p>At command has a utility called <code>atq</code> that can be used to list at jobs that are pending execution.<br>To simply list the at jobs, run;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-125" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>atq</code></pre><p>If there are any jobs pending execution, you will see them on the output;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-160" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>atq</code></pre><pre class="wp-block-code"><code>31  Mon Dec  2 23:00:00 2019 a root
33  Sun Oct  6 16:00:00 2019 a root
32  Fri Sep 13 00:00:00 2019 a root
</code></pre><p>Similarly, you can use at command with <code>-l</code> option.<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at -l</code></pre><h3 class="wp-block-heading">Delete Scheduled at jobs</h3><p>Scheduled at jobs can be removed using the <code>atrm</code> utility or by passing option <code>-r</code> to at command.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-914" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="914"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-161" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>atr -r &lt;JOB ID&gt;<job number as shown by atq></job></code></pre><p>or</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-711" data-method="ai-placeholders" class="ezoic-autoinsert-ad"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="711"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>atrm &lt;JOB ID&gt;<job number as shown by atq></job></code></pre><p>For example, based on the output of the <code>atq</code> command above, you can remove at job with job number 31 using the command;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at -r 31</code></pre><p>or</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-162" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>atrm 31</code></pre><p>To remove all the jobs in the queue, simply obtain the job numbers and remove them as follows;<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>atrm $(atq | cut -f1)</code></pre><p>There are other options that are aliased to <code>atrm</code> command.<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at -d &lt;JOB ID&gt;</code></pre><h3 class="wp-block-heading">Print Listed At Jobs to STDOUT</h3><p>To print listed at jobs to standard output, simply use the command;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-915" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="915"></span><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-163" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at -c &lt;JOB ID&gt;</code></pre><p>For example, to cat the at job number 23 to standard output.<pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>at -c 23</code></pre><h3 class="wp-block-heading">Controlling Access to At</h3><p>It is also possible to control who can run at jobs using the <code>/etc/at.allow</code> and <code>/etc/at.deny</code> files.<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>only users listed in the <code>at.allow</code> file are allowed to use <code>at</code><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-164" data-inserter-version="2"></span><li>users listed in <code>at.deny</code> file are not allowed to use <code>at</code>.</ul><h3 class="wp-block-heading">Using batch command</h3><p>Another command almost similar to at command is <code>batch</code> command. This command is used to schedule tasks that can only be executed when system load drops below 1.5 or any value specified in<br>Batch command does not accepts any parameters and runs interactively.</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-916" data-method="placement-service"></span><span data-ez-ph-id="916"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>batch
at&gt;</code></pre><p>For example to execute the script, <code>/home/me/myscripts/clean-tmp.sh</code>, simply run <code>batch</code> command and enter the script at the <code>at</code> prompt.<br>Press Ctrl+d once you are done typing commands;</p><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-165" data-inserter-version="2"></span><pre class="wp-block-preformatted"><code>batch
at&gt; /home/me/myscripts/clean-tmp.sh
at&gt; <eot></eot></code></pre><p><code>batch</code> command is no longer maintained on most Linux/Unix distributions.<p>Read more about <code>at</code> command on <code>man at</code>.</div><footer class="entry-meta" aria-label="Entry meta"><span class="tags-links"><span class="gp-icon icon-tags"><svg viewBox="0 0 512 512" aria-hidden="true" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em"><path d="M20 39.5c-8.836 0-16 7.163-16 16v176c0 4.243 1.686 8.313 4.687 11.314l224 224c6.248 6.248 16.378 6.248 22.626 0l176-176c6.244-6.244 6.25-16.364.013-22.615l-223.5-224A15.999 15.999 0 00196.5 39.5H20zm56 96c0-13.255 10.745-24 24-24s24 10.745 24 24-10.745 24-24 24-24-10.745-24-24z"></path><path d="M259.515 43.015c4.686-4.687 12.284-4.687 16.97 0l228 228c4.686 4.686 4.686 12.284 0 16.97l-180 180c-4.686 4.687-12.284 4.687-16.97 0-4.686-4.686-4.686-12.284 0-16.97L479.029 279.5 259.515 59.985c-4.686-4.686-4.686-12.284 0-16.97z"></path></svg></span><span class="screen-reader-text">Tags </span><a href="https://kifarunix.com/tag/at/" rel="tag">at</a>, <a href="https://kifarunix.com/tag/at-jobs/" rel="tag">at jobs</a>, <a href="https://kifarunix.com/tag/batch/" rel="tag">batch</a></span></footer></div></article><div class="gb-container gb-container-77635d6a"><h2 class="wp-block-heading has-text-align-center has-base-3-color has-text-color">SUPPORT US VIA A VIRTUAL CUP OF COFFEE</h2><p class="has-text-align-center has-base-3-color has-text-color" style="font-size:22px">We're passionate about sharing our knowledge and experiences with you through our blog. Enabling/Disabling Startup Programs:**\n   - Select a startup application, and at the bottom, an option to disable or enable will appear.\n   - Disable unnecessary applications to streamline the startup process.\n\n**4. In the video, approximately 15 startup applications are shown, with 12 set to run in the background during boot.\n   - Check the Notification Area to identify applications that are currently running.\n\n**5. Boosting Startup Speed:**\n   - Disabling unnecessary startup applications can significantly reduce boot time. Consider the cumulative impact of multiple applications loading at startup.\n   - View the file location of selected applications to understand their resource consumption. Navigate to the \u0026#34;Details\u0026#34; tab for detailed system resource information.\n\n**6. Freeing Up System Resources:**\n   - By disabling unnecessary startup applications, not only do you speed up boot times, but you also free up system resources for other applications to use.\n\n**7. Caution with Anti-Virus Software:**\n   - Exercise caution when disabling startup applications, particularly those related to antivirus software. Ensure essential security applications remain enabled.\n\n**8. User Choice:**\n   - The decision of which applications to run on system startup is in your hands. Customize your startup programs based on your preferences and needs.\n\n**Conclusion:**\n   - Managing startup programs is a simple yet effective way to optimize your Windows startup experience.\n   -
